% ── C14 ─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────
@article{Demerouti2025,
  author    = {Demerouti, Evangelia},
  title     = {Job demands-resources and conservation of resources
               theories: {How} do they help to explain employee
               well-being and future job design?},
  journal   = {Journal of Business Research},
  year      = {2025},
  volume    = {192},
  pages     = {115296},
  doi       = {10.1016/j.jbusres.2025.115296},
  url       = {https://doi.org/10.1016/j.jbusres.2025.115296},
  note      = {Open access CC BY 4.0. Theoretical review; JBR 50th
               anniversary special issue; single-authored by JD-R
               theory co-originator. Compares COR (Hobfoll 1989)
               and JD-R (Demerouti et al. 2001) on 8 similarities
               and 7 key differences (Table 1). JD-R 7 propositions:
               P1 resources aid goals/reduce demands; P2 dual process
               (health impairment: demands\(\rightarrow\)burnout;
               motivational: resources\(\rightarrow\)engagement);
               P3 buffering + boosting hypotheses; P4-P5 personal
               resources; P6 gain cycle (engagement\(\rightarrow\)job
               crafting); P7 loss cycle (strain\(\rightarrow\)self-
               undermining). Key distinctions for hybrid work:
               employee-led flexibility=resource; employer-led=demand
               (Kattenbach et al. 2010). Resource substitution
               hypothesis (Ross\&Mirowsky 2010). Resource caravan
               passageways. Tipping points for resources. Future job
               design: dynamic, proactive, human-centred, prospective
               (Table 3). Meta-analytic support cited: Alarcon 2011
               (burnout); Mazzetti 2023 (engagement); Lesener 2019
               (reciprocal). Eindhoven Univ. Technology, Netherlands.
               JBR Vol.192 2025.},
}

  author    = {Curzi, Ylenia and Scapolan, Anna Chiara and Ferrarini,
               Filippo},
  title     = {Redesigning performance management practices to boost
               innovative behaviours: the moderating role of remote
               work},
  journal   = {International Journal of Organizational Analysis},
  year      = {2026},
  volume    = {34},
  number    = {12},
  pages     = {53--71},
  doi       = {10.1108/IJOA-03-2025-5320},
  url       = {https://doi.org/10.1108/IJOA-03-2025-5320},
  note      = {Open access CC BY 4.0. OLS regression; n=647;
               Italy; cross-sectional 2022; convenience sample.
               Signalling Theory of HRM. PM practices \(\times\) remote
               work moderation on IWB (\(\alpha\)=0.90). Continuous
               feedback: only PM practice that significantly drives IWB
               at high remote work (\(\beta\)=0.196, p\(\leq\)0.05).
               Goal setting involvement and training opportunities
               lose IWB effect remotely (training
               \(\beta_{\text{interaction}}\)=-0.493, p\(\leq\)0.05).
               Result-based and new-competence-based appraisal support
               IWB regardless of remote work extent. FLAG: convenience
               sample; most IVs dichotomised; IWB \(\neq\) productivity.
               University of Modena and Reggio Emilia, Italy.
               Emerald IJOA Vol.34 No.12 2026.},
}

% ── B10 ─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────
@article{Mele2023,
  author    = {Mele, Valentina and Belardinelli, Paolo and Bell{\'{e}},
               Nicola},
  title     = {Telework in public organizations: {A} systematic review
               and research agenda},
  journal   = {Public Administration Review},
  year      = {2023},
  volume    = {83},
  number    = {6},
  pages     = {1649--1666},
  doi       = {10.1111/puar.13734},
  url       = {https://doi.org/10.1111/puar.13734},
  note      = {Open access CC BY-NC-ND. PRISMA SLR; 120 studies;
               Web of Science; up to May 2023. Public sector focus.
               Four-dimension framework: space, time, ICT,
               autonomy. Antecedents: supportive leadership (8/12+),
               individual productivity (11/13+). Effects: productivity
               conflicting (12+/4-/3 null, 19 studies); WLB
               predominantly positive (11/17); turnover reduction
               (11/16); professional isolation consistent negative
               (5/5). Africa (excl. SA) and nonprofit/NGO gap
               confirmed. Data: Harvard Dataverse.
               Bocconi/Indiana/Sant'Anna. PAR journal.},
}

% ── B09 ─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────
@article{OBrady2025,
  author    = {O'Brady, Sean and Doellgast, Virginia and Starcevic,
               Jelena},
  title     = {Worker voice and mutual gains from remote performance
               management: {Evidence} from digitalized services in
               {North America} and {Germany}},
  journal   = {Human Resource Management Journal},
  year      = {2025},
  volume    = {35},
  pages     = {864--878},
  doi       = {10.1111/1748-8583.12601},
  url       = {https://doi.org/10.1111/1748-8583.12601},
  note      = {Open access CC BY 4.0. Qualitative comparative; 250
               respondents; 26 CBAs; 11 telecoms firms; Canada/US/
               Germany; 2021--2024. JD-R + pluralist ER theory.
               Monitoring as demand; coaching as resource; mutual gains
               = balance via collective voice/CBAs. Germany (works
               council co-determination) >> North America in monitoring
               constraints and developmental coaching. Management
               systems (not remote work per se) determine performance
               outcomes. McMaster University and Cornell University.
               Funded: SSHRC (Canada) and AFL-CIO Tech Institute.},
}

% ── B08 ─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────
@article{Tonnessen2026,
  author    = {T{\o}nnessen, {\O}ystein and Baah-Peprah, Prince and
               Fl{\aa}ten, Bj{\o}rn-Tore and Larsen, Thomas Bj{\o}rnson},
  title     = {Managerial insights into trust, control, and performance
               in remote work environments},
  journal   = {Journal of Business Research},
  year      = {2026},
  volume    = {215},
  pages     = {116323},
  doi       = {10.1016/j.jbusres.2026.116323},
  url       = {https://doi.org/10.1016/j.jbusres.2026.116323},
  note      = {Open access CC BY 4.0. CB-SEM (lavaan R; Satorra-Bentler
               robust ML); n=288 managers/8,351 employees; US; 2022.
               IV: manager-employee trust + remote work possibility.
               Mediators: formal control (outcome) + informal control
               (self-control). Moderator: requirements risk.
               H5b supported: informal control mediates RW->performance
               (\(\beta\)=0.062, p<0.01). H5a rejected: formal control
               does not mediate. H6: informal control > formal
               control on performance (\(\Delta\beta\)=0.628,
               Z=12.498). Requirements risk negatively affects
               performance (\(\beta\)=-0.285) and attenuates informal
               control effectiveness. FLAG: ICO AVE=0.41 below 0.50.
               FLAG: authors explicitly caution against applying to
               Nigeria (low-trust context). University of Agder, Norway.
               Available online 30 May 2026.},
}

% ── B07 ─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────
@article{AlSuwaidi2025,
  author    = {Al-Suwaidi, Khalifa and Alsyouf, Imad and Tahboub, Zain
               and Alsaad, Abdallah and Alsyouf, Adi},
  title     = {Integrating fourth industrial revolution technologies in
               human resource practices: {Mediating} roles of work
               flexibility, quality of work life, and distributive
               fairness in enhancing employee productivity},
  journal   = {Sustainable Futures},
  year      = {2025},
  volume    = {10},
  pages     = {101150},
  doi       = {10.1016/j.sftr.2025.101150},
  url       = {https://doi.org/10.1016/j.sftr.2025.101150},
  note      = {Open access CC BY 4.0. PLS-SEM (PLSc/SmartPLS4);
               n=533; Sharjah UAE public sector; cross-sectional 2024.
               4IR (computing/digitalising/integrating) as IV.
               Three mediators: FWA (\(\beta_{\text{indirect}}\)=0.110),
               QWL (\(\beta_{\text{indirect}}\)=0.222, strongest),
               distributive fairness (\(\beta_{\text{indirect}}\)=0.059).
               R\textsuperscript{2}=57.7\% for productivity. All
               Cronbach's \(\alpha\geq 0.874\). CMB checked (VIF<3.3).
               FLAG: \(\beta\) discrepancies between abstract and Table
               5/6 -- use Table 5/6 values for citation.
               University of Sharjah, UAE.},
}

% ── B06 ─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────
@article{Lauring2025,
  author    = {Lauring, Jakob and Jonasson, Charlotte},
  title     = {What is hybrid work? {Towards} greater conceptual
               clarity of a common term and understanding its
               consequences},
  journal   = {Human Resource Management Review},
  year      = {2025},
  volume    = {35},
  number    = {1},
  pages     = {101044},
  doi       = {10.1016/j.hrmr.2024.101044},
  url       = {https://doi.org/10.1016/j.hrmr.2024.101044},
  note      = {Open access CC BY 4.0. Conceptual review; 62 articles;
               Scopus + EBSCO BSC. Aarhus University, Denmark.
               Defines hybrid work as ongoing dynamic switches across
               modality (analog/digital), location (office/distributed),
               and temporality (constrained/asynchronous). Three-level
               taxonomy (Table 3). Nomological network (Fig. 1).
               Structuration Theory (Giddens). THESIS Ch. 2.1
               definitional anchor. Published online 28 August 2024.},
}

% ── B05 ─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────
@article{Maity2025,
  author    = {Maity, Richik and Lee, Khai Loon},
  title     = {The impact of remote and hybrid work models on small
               and medium-sized enterprises productivity: a systematic
               literature review},
  journal   = {SN Business \& Economics},
  year      = {2025},
  volume    = {5},
  doi       = {10.1007/s43546-025-00931-7},
  url       = {https://doi.org/10.1007/s43546-025-00931-7},
  note      = {Open access CC BY-NC-ND 4.0. PRISMA 2020 SLR; 12 studies;
               11 countries; Scopus + WoS; 2020--2024. Universiti Malaysia
               Pahang (UMPSA). FRGS-funded. Conditional productivity
               thesis: FWA → productivity contingent on digital
               infrastructure + management practices + WLB + org
               readiness. Four-pillar framework (Table 2). No SSA
               primary study in final sample (Africa gap confirmed).
               Published online 26 September 2025.},
}
